  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b30dff02-4bbd-45e1-8a1d-7dc22031e3c3'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText1847312518273232121" style="display:none">Whistling Tor is a place of secrets, a mysterious, wooded hill housing the crumbling fortress of a chieftain whose name is spoken throughout the district in tones of revulsion and bitterness. A curse lies over Anluan's family and his people; those woods hold a perilous force whose every whisper threatens doom.<br /><br />For young scribe Caitrin it is a safe haven. This place where nobody else is prepared to go seems exactly what she needs, for Caitrin is fleeing her own demons. As Caitrin comes to know Anluan and his home in more depth she realizes that it is only through her love and determination that the curse can be broken and Anluan and his people set free.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139439996" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139439996?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139439996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7671160292355690751">It is a well-known fact that I adore Beauty and the Beast retellings, so it's about damn time I reviewed this. It is not only the best retelling I have ever read, it is among my <b>top five favorite books of all time.</b> I can't even tell you how beautiful, fantastic, magical this story is. It truly has everything. It is a long story; don't be afraid of the length. It will fly by as you're immersed in it, and I, for one, wish it were longer. Also, the "Beast" is a long red-haired Irish dude with half </span>
  <span id="freeText7671160292355690751" style="display:none">It is a well-known fact that I adore Beauty and the Beast retellings, so it's about damn time I reviewed this. It is not only the best retelling I have ever read, it is among my <b>top five favorite books of all time.</b> I can't even tell you how beautiful, fantastic, magical this story is. It truly has everything. It is a long story; don't be afraid of the length. It will fly by as you're immersed in it, and I, for one, wish it were longer. Also, the "Beast" is a long red-haired Irish dude with half his face kinda paralyzed and so in my mind I'm imagining the other half to look like this.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491318973i/22397674._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>HHHHHHHHNNNNNNNNNNNGGGGGGGGG<br><br>I don't have to summarize <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> to you. This book is about a lovely girl, named <b>Caitrin</b>. An orphan. I know, an orphan. It sounds cliché; i assure you it is not. It is about pain, suffering; mental and physical abuse. A girl whose beauty is used to shame and abuse her into submission.<blockquote>
  <i>Ita spoke in my head, her voice a derisory whisper: See the way men look at you? You’re made to be a whore, Caitrin. Be thankful Cillian wants to wed you.Without him you’d be headed down a path to ruin.</i>
</blockquote>There is no explicit violence in this book, but rest assured that its ghost is very much alive in our protagonist's mind and defines who she is.<blockquote>
  <i> The bruises on my skin—blue, black, yellow, an angry patchwork—would fade. There were other hurts, deeper ones, that would be harder to lose. You did it, Caitrin, I reminded myself. You got up and walked out.</i>
</blockquote>Her escape is where our book begins. We are in a time long ago and far away, when the Norman conquests were taking place in Ireland. Caitrin is a girl on the run, terrified of being found. Penniless, with only the clothes on her back and the tool she carries with her; she has been well-trained by her father as a scribe. It is how she hopes to earn a living and escape her would-be captors.<br><br>She wanders into a strange place called <b>Whistling Tors.</b> A place whose nearby villagers regard with fear and superstition. A place with a fearful and cursed chieftain, whose neglect of his duties and cursed appearance makes him a reviled personage to his people. Caitrin hears that he might need a scribe. It may be the last place in the world she wants to be, but it may also be safe refuge, and really, she has no choice.<br><br>The rumors about Whistling Tors are not false. If anything, they were grossly underexaggerated. The woods is filled with <b>ghostly spectres</b> who haunt your every step.<blockquote>
  <i>“Oh God, oh God!” someone screamed, as behind the rider a swirling mass flowed out from under the trees around the courtyard, not mist, not smoke, but something full of gaping mouths and clutching hands, something with a hundred shrieking, moaning voices and a hundred creeping, pattering feet.</i>
</blockquote>The <b>Beast</b> is a young chieftain named <b>Anluan</b>, who is tortured by his fate, something through no fault of his. The romance is such a <b>slow burn</b>, and it is <b>a joy to watch friendship and love blossom between them</b>. Romance is there, but I assure you it is <b>subtle and believable</b>.<blockquote>
  <i>“I hardly know what to say.” Anluan spoke with some awkwardness, as if he thought his words might offend me. “Your kinsman was right when he called me a cripple. I cannot ride, I cannot run, I cannot lead an army into battle. Not an army made up of earthly warriors of Magnus’s kind, anyway. But this force I can command. On Whistling Tor, the host is obedient to my will. While you stay here, I can keep you safe. I hope you will stay, Caitrin, now that you know the truth. We want you here. We need you.”</i>
</blockquote>Love and lust are written beautifully.<br><br>There is a great mystery to be solved, a mystery that holds the key to freedom for Anluan and his living retainers, as well as the spectral ones, who are not merely malevolent spirits.<blockquote>
  <i> When Anluan had brought them rushing to my aid they had screamed, wailed, assaulted the ears. Now they were utterly silent. Not creatures of ancient legend; not devils or demons. All the same, my skin prickled as I looked at them: here a woman carrying an injured child, there an old man with a heavy bag over his shoulder, his back bent, his limbs shaking; under an oak, a younger man whose fingers clutched feverishly onto an amulet strung around his neck. There were warriors and priests here, little girls and old women. The more I gazed at them, turning to look on all sides, the more of them appeared, until the forest was full of them. Ghosts? Spirits?</i>
</blockquote>There are no magical wardrobes and candlesticks here. There is, however, a giant ghostly hound, a spectral monk, creatures from beyond time, and <b>more dark magic than you can shake a stick at</b>. This book has everything, and I truly come to love every single character in the book, <b>living or dead.</b><br><br>The elements of Beauty and the Beast are there; the rose, in this case a rare flower called Heart's Blood, and the magic mirror, in this instance much more sinister than the original. They are interwoven into the tale so well that it hardly feels like a retelling at all; there is nothing forced about it. The characterization and development is amazing, and the real-world conflicts are interspersed with the magical, making this such a <b>spectacular read.</b> It is a story of hope. This is quite likely <b>the best retelling of all time</b> and I beg you to read it.<br><br>Read more reviews at <a href="http://www.theallitterates.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alliterates</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7671160292355690751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_129762191" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129762191" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129762191?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=leaves-awesomeness-behind">leaves-awesomeness-behind</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=australian-writer">australian-writer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129762191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16321616910276854720">Marquis de Sade is a rather famous figure. Mostly for a lot of kinky sex acts because all of his sex fantasies included violence, criminality and blasphemy. That and he really liked buttsecks!<br/><br/>Okay, so history remembers Marquis de Sade for the crazy, deviant man that he was. But I think we're all forgetting the real point to the story of Marquis de Sade... and that is love. Love that conquors all. Love that supports and love that understands and accepts. After all, the Marquis de Sade had a very </span>
  <span id="freeText16321616910276854720" style="display:none">Marquis de Sade is a rather famous figure. Mostly for a lot of kinky sex acts because all of his sex fantasies included violence, criminality and blasphemy. That and he really liked buttsecks!<br><br>Okay, so history remembers Marquis de Sade for the crazy, deviant man that he was. But I think we're all forgetting the real point to the story of Marquis de Sade... and that is love. Love that conquors all. Love that supports and love that understands and accepts. After all, the Marquis de Sade had a very lovely religious wife, Renee-Pelagie de Montreuil who was always there to organize his orgies, hustle is prostitutes, bitch slap the hired help who tried to complain of the sexual and physical abuse being wrought out against them and also to break him out of jail.<br><br>All of this while completely understanding that it was IMPORTANT for him to bone her sister on the side.<br><br>That, my friends, is love!<br><br><br>I've heard people complain that there isn't a strong romance in this book and I actually can't understand why. I found the romance in this book to be powerful, beautiful and touching. I truly felt that Anluan and Caitrin were perfect for each other. Just like Marquis de Sade and Renee-Pelagie de Montreuil were perfect for each other(no, I'm just jokin' y'all. Caitrin and Anluan made a beautiful couple!)<br><br>The creepy atmosphere of this story was so well executed, the castle and its occupants so seemingly alive that I felt true remorse when the story came to an end.<br><br>Though the mystery was painfully obvious right from the get-go, I never actually felt the sense that Caitrin was particularly slow on the uptake - just that she was a trusting, good person with a lot on her mind and a lot of distractions.<br><br>As a retake on the Beauty and the Beast tale, this one was both beautifully done and very, very PC.<br><br>Caitrin is not kidnapped and is not a victim, nor is Anluan an actual beast though his short temper and deformity are quite realistic.<br><br>This is the second book by Juliet Marillier that I have ever read and she's been consistently thoughtful and conscience about her prose, her message and her characterization. <br><br>I honestly look forward to reading more books by her.<br><br>I also honestly look forward to surpassing her in the 'Most Followed' category for Australia! Suck it, Marillier! I'll get you one day!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380341203i/697445.jpg" alt="awesome" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_129719512" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129719512" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129719512?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451462930" href="/book/show/6391467-heart-s-blood">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129719512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6109929926268098007">I think <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier' title='Juliet Marillier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Juliet Marillier</a>'s most successful books are the ones that follow traditional fairy tales the closest. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6278019.Heart_s_Blood__Whistling_Tor___1_' title='Heart's Blood (Whistling Tor, #1) by Juliet Marillier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heart's Blood</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13928.Daughter_of_the_Forest__Sevenwaters___1_' title='Daughter of the Forest (Sevenwaters, #1) by Juliet Marillier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Daughter of the Forest</a> are the best of hers I've read so far.<br/><br/>And as far as fairy tale retelling goes, nobody does it as well as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier' title='Juliet Marillier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Juliet Marillier</a> does. She has that special ability to take a centuries-old tale and fill it with interesting new characters, historical details, original and always very atmospheric setting - and voila, a great story that doesn't feel like an</span>
  <span id="freeText6109929926268098007" style="display:none">I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier" title="Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Juliet Marillier</a>'s most successful books are the ones that follow traditional fairy tales the closest. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6278019.Heart_s_Blood__Whistling_Tor___1_" title="Heart's Blood (Whistling Tor, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Heart's Blood</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13928.Daughter_of_the_Forest__Sevenwaters___1_" title="Daughter of the Forest (Sevenwaters, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Daughter of the Forest</a> are the best of hers I've read so far.<br /><br />And as far as fairy tale retelling goes, nobody does it as well as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier" title="Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Juliet Marillier</a> does. She has that special ability to take a centuries-old tale and fill it with interesting new characters, historical details, original and always very atmospheric setting - and voila, a great story that doesn't feel like an old tired rip-off at all.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6278019.Heart_s_Blood__Whistling_Tor___1_" title="Heart's Blood (Whistling Tor, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Heart's Blood</a> is a fresh take on <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> and probably the most successful reinvisioning of this story I've come across. The plot is familiar - a pretty girl, a beastly-looking man, a curse, a flower, an enchanted castle. You all know it. But the characters are fresh - Caitrin is a scribe escaping from her abusive relatives, Anluan is a young man suffering from palsy whose family was cursed decades ago. The story is set in Ireland. Whistling Tor is an enchanted, misty place full of sleepless ghosts...<br /><br />The main challenge of any <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> retelling is to make us believe in a deep connection and love between a pretty girl and an ugly, best-like man. I remember reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5339.Robin_McKinley" title="Robin McKinley" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin McKinley</a>'s version and never feeling why and when the two main characters fell in love. Not so in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6278019.Heart_s_Blood__Whistling_Tor___1_" title="Heart's Blood (Whistling Tor, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Heart's Blood</a>. The way Caitrin and Anluan's relationship is written makes you truly believe in their love for each other. And even more, in their mutual sexual attraction. No small fit, considering that Anluan is pretty much a cripple. <br /><br />There is also this great way these two communicate I found very appealing - they do not try to change each other, but help one another to overcome their weaknesses and hang-ups, to realize how much they have to offer, to become more confident, stronger. Very touching. <br /><br />My only problem, the usual with all <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier" title="Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Juliet Marillier</a>'s books, is that she tends to be too wordy. Very often I feel like whatever needs to be said could have been said in fewer words. I found myself particularly frustrated in the end of the story, when all exciting stuff started happening and it was slowed down by wordiness. I skim-read a lot at that point to get to the juicy stuff.<br /><br />I see that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6278019.Heart_s_Blood__Whistling_Tor___1_" title="Heart's Blood (Whistling Tor, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Heart's Blood</a> is the first book <i>Whistling Tor</i> series. I wonder what else is there to say about this place. What future books are going to be about? Does anyone know?</span>
  <a data-text-id="6109929926268098007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1161135862" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1161135862" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1161135862?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=in-a-minority-here">in-a-minority-here</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fairytales">fairytales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1161135862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15594280803096588259"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448833642i/17195408._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b><u>Actual rating</u> : 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Trust me, I wanted to love this book so, so much. But if <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6278019.Heart_s_Blood' title='Heart's Blood by Juliet Marillier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heart's Blood</a> casted a spell on me</b>, captivating me, I encountered the same problems I had with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8452340.Shadowfell__Shadowfell___1_' title='Shadowfell (Shadowfell, #1) by Juliet Marillier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadowfell</a>, making it hard to entirely connect with the story, especially in the second half. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448833642i/17195409._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>✔ <u>
  <b>Fascinating settings</b>
</u> : Think about an ominous forest, a mysterious castle, whose inhabitants have been suffering from a curse for years. What not to love? <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448833642i/17195410._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>If I wasn't completely won by the writing (I'll come back to that), </span>
  <span id="freeText15594280803096588259" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448833642i/17195408._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><u>Actual rating</u> : 3.5 stars</b><br><br>Trust me, I wanted to love this book so, so much. But if <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6278019.Heart_s_Blood" title="Heart's Blood by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Heart's Blood</a> casted a spell on me</b>, captivating me, I encountered the same problems I had with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8452340.Shadowfell__Shadowfell___1_" title="Shadowfell (Shadowfell, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadowfell</a>, making it hard to entirely connect with the story, especially in the second half. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448833642i/17195409._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✔ <u>
  <b>Fascinating settings</b>
</u> : Think about an ominous forest, a mysterious castle, whose inhabitants have been suffering from a curse for years. What not to love? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448833642i/17195410._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If I wasn't completely won by the writing (I'll come back to that), I can't deny that the descriptions were beautifully crafted and so <i>vivid</i>, it felt as if I was there. <br><br>✔ <u>An <b>intriguing plot</b></u> : <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> is (shockingly, lol) one of my favorite fairytales of all times, yet its retellings rarely manage to capture the magical enthrallment I felt the first time I read Beaumont's tale, and I've grown to resent and avoid them, to be honest. The fact is, either they're too close to the original (but boring) or they're so twisted that I can't recognize anything. None of this here. <b>If the story turns let me bewildered (in a good way), <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier" title="Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Juliet Marillier</a> included several aspects as winks to the fairytale reader and I loved that</b>. <br><br>From the underlying darkness threatening every turn, to the longing oozing from every page, I flew through the first half, enchanted. <br><br>✔ <u>A <b>well-developed and complex cast of characters</b></u> : <br><br>► <b>Caitrin is a wonderful and relatable heroine</b> : after having been abused by her family after her father's death, she finds the courage to flee and is constantly testing her strength. She's by no means our kickass/soul eating warrior, yet she <i>is</i> strong, in her not so flashy way. <br><br>► <b>Anluan is a crippled, cursed man whose anger issues would have infuriated me if his character wasn't so multi-layered, so <i>complex</i></b>. Please don't judge him too fast : he can be maddening, but he's not violent and so, so loyal. The despair of this awkward, self-loathing man who hides behind his grumpiness moved me. So burdened and tortured, unable to see that life can be <i>more</i>. <br><br>► <b>As for the other inhabitants of Whistling Tor, what can I say except that I loved them all?</b> From Magnus the kind soldier to Eirith the crazy monk, they all add something magical to the story and I couldn't help but draw parallels with the Beast hilarious and endearing companions. <br><br>✔ The <b>romance is believable, light and straights-on wonderful</b>. They made me <i>squeal</i>. I know! GAH. They gradually learn to trust each others', to overlook the appearances and their fears.<br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448833642i/17195411._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unfortunately there was a counter spell. Sigh.<br><br>✘ Trust me, <b>I don't mind a little predictability... Until I reach the point when it influences (in a bad way) what I think about a MC</b>. Sadly, it was the case here. It took Caitrin so much time before solving the mystery (IN SPITE OF ALL THESE EVIDENCES EVERYWHERE), it drove me nuts. See, I understand that she's willing to trust, but come on. This is too-much. From the moment I figured it all (way too fast) I grew restless, then annoyed, even if I didn't want to be. I was constantly making excuses for her lack of judgment, until the moment I COULDN'T. <br><br>✘ While I realize that it's a prevalent trope in fairytales, in my opinion <b>the hope talk grew old pretty fast</b>. Hope will prevail. Because Hope is the key. Don't you believe that? Have you understood how important hope is? Do you? Do you? Are you sure? Because I'm going to repeat it over and over again. Oh. My. <i>GOSH</i>. <br> <br>✘ As I said earlier, if I appreciated how beautiful the descriptions were, <b>it remains that the writing was often too wordy for me</b>. I'm by no means an action lover, but it was so frustrating sometimes that I had a hard time not to skim. Indeed some parts.... dragged....<i>so much</i>...that I couldn't help but be <b>bored</b>, unfortunately, and yes, I wanted the author to go to the freaking point. <br><br>► That's why it sort of lost its magic by the end. Way too long in my opinion, and yet I'll still keep a fond memory of Whistling Tor and its unusual inhabitants. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8789462858225751065">This is definitely my favorite of Juliet Marillier's books, but to be fair, it's only my second. <br/><br/>That being said, it wasn't a love at first sight, much like the main character in this Beauty and the Beast retelling. It grew on me, much as the Beast grew on Belle.<br/><br/>The later half was quite exciting and full of magic and trying to break the curse and there was plenty of ghosts and ghouls and armies and all the awesome Norman invasion historical stuff to keep me involved in the medieval world this dr</span>
  <span id="freeText8789462858225751065" style="display:none">This is definitely my favorite of Juliet Marillier's books, but to be fair, it's only my second. <br /><br />That being said, it wasn't a love at first sight, much like the main character in this Beauty and the Beast retelling. It grew on me, much as the Beast grew on Belle.<br /><br />The later half was quite exciting and full of magic and trying to break the curse and there was plenty of ghosts and ghouls and armies and all the awesome Norman invasion historical stuff to keep me involved in the medieval world this draws from. All the characters became something special for me, too, thanks to the weight of their interactions and involvement with each other.<br /><br />Unfortunately, it took a while for me to get there. I was kinda bored by the pacing of at least the first half and while it was really focused on the realism angle and strove hard to stick to reality in the retelling, I was only very mildly interested. It was halfway between a historical and a slice-of-life with mild hidden past. It took a while to build up to something cool.<br /><br />Even so, it ended nicely and it was still charming.</span>

<div id="review_1034983511" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1034983511" />
    <a title="♛Tash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5451856-tash"><img alt="♛Tash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456286012p2/5451856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1034983511?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♛Tash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♛Tash" href="/user/show/5451856-tash">♛Tash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330451123" href="/book/show/8033148-heart-s-blood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5451856-tash?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5451856-tash?shelf=on-hand">on-hand</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5451856-tash?shelf=fairytale-retelling">fairytale-retelling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1034983511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9091200610759738435"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435946526ra/15396226.gif' width='304' height='171' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><p></p><br/><b>Warning: this is a gushy review, so if you don't want to be embarrassed on my behalf, turn away now.</b><br/><br/>The story opens with Caitrin, our beauty in this BatB retelling, running away from her abusive guardian as far as money can take her. She goes as far as Whistling Tor, more on Whistling Tor later. Desperate, Caitrin takes a summer job as scribe to the reclusive lord of Whistling Tor, despite the discouragement of the local folk. She's determinedly positive (irritatingly so at times) to complete he</span>
  <span id="freeText9091200610759738435" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435946526ra/15396226.gif" width="304" height="171" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><p></p><br><b>Warning: this is a gushy review, so if you don't want to be embarrassed on my behalf, turn away now.</b><br><br>The story opens with Caitrin, our beauty in this BatB retelling, running away from her abusive guardian as far as money can take her. She goes as far as Whistling Tor, more on Whistling Tor later. Desperate, Caitrin takes a summer job as scribe to the reclusive lord of Whistling Tor, despite the discouragement of the local folk. She's determinedly positive (irritatingly so at times) to complete her work and help everyone in the household, despite the scary shit going on.<br><br>There are no beastly beasts here, only Anluan. He's physically deformed, he's prickly and given to outbursts, and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he reluctantly commands the host, an army of the undead. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Anluan is an exceptional character, he is flawed in almost all facets, and in a genre dominated by perfect males who can make love on top of a horse while slaying a dragon, it's refreshing. Besides from the physical deformities and weakness, he is just as naive, or more so,than Caitrin.<br><br>The romance, ah the romance! I loved every minute of the awkward flirtation, if you can call it that. Caitrin realizes that she's crushing on Anluan the day after she meets him, so naturally she had to teach him how to do calligraphy because she's got game. She holds his hand the first few strokes, while he writes her name on the parchment over and over. She blushes, he blushes - just adorable!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435944910i/15395887.jpg" width="236" height="174" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Best thing about the romance in this book is that it never takes center stage, it is there, but it just doesn't run over more important plot lines. <br><br>The rest of the characters in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6278019.Heart_s_Blood" title="Heart's Blood by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Heart's Blood</a> are brilliantly drawn, I fell in love with all of them, so the ending, although heartbreaking, is apropos and touching.<br><br>The setting, Whistling Tor, is just perfect for a BatB retelling. Located high up on the hills of Connacht (that's Western Ireland for us history noobs), Whistling Tor is isolated, eternally misty and surrounded by a dark forest, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[haunted by the above-mentioned host, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.It is definitely not included in Connacht's tourism brochure.<br><br>Needless to say I loved this BatB retelling, the best among I've read so far. Juliet Marillier's prose is poetic and graceful, and the language fitting.<br><br><i>“He was seated on the bench now. He had his left elbow on his knee, his right arm across his lap, his shoulders hunched, his head bowed. White face, red hair: snow and fire, like something from an old tale. The book I had noticed earlier was on the bench beside him, its covers shut. Around Anluan's feet and in the birdbath, small visitors to the garden hopped and splashed and made the most of the day that was becoming fair and sunny. He did not seem to notice them. As for me, I found it difficult to take my eyes from him. There was an odd beauty in his isolation and his sadness, like that of a forlorn prince ensorcelled by a wicked enchantress, or a traveller lost forever in a world far from home.”</i><br><br>The plot moves gradually without being dragging, the action and the "slow" parts well-proportioned.<br><br><br><b>TL; DR : Tash adores this book to pieces</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9091200610759738435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2525349591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2525349591" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2525349591?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=witches-warlocks-and-magic">witches-warlocks-and-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=romantasy">romantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=beautifully-broken-bastards">beautifully-broken-bastards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bb-b-2018">bb-b-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2525349591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16983442396631608536">This isn’t really a Beauty and the Beast retelling but it reminded me very loosely of one. Again, Juliet Marillier delivers a book that has the distinctive feel of an old school fairytale. There is a curse, a castle, a semi-disfigured man, a strong heroine with nowhere else to turn and mirrors that don’t reflect the world but have other things moving inside of them. It was bound to call out to me just waiting to be read.<br/><blockquote>
  <i>There was an odd beauty in his isolation and his sadness, like that of a </i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText16983442396631608536" style="display:none">This isn’t really a Beauty and the Beast retelling but it reminded me very loosely of one. Again, Juliet Marillier delivers a book that has the distinctive feel of an old school fairytale. There is a curse, a castle, a semi-disfigured man, a strong heroine with nowhere else to turn and mirrors that don’t reflect the world but have other things moving inside of them. It was bound to call out to me just waiting to be read.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>There was an odd beauty in his isolation and his sadness, like that of a forlorn prince ensorcelled by a wicked enchantress, or a traveler lost forever in a world far from home.</i>
</blockquote><br />Caitlin is a scribe in a world where female scribes aren’t accepted. She has worked with her father her entire life and is great at what she does. Her father has passed her work off as his own due to social convention but upon his death she has nowhere to turn and the family that should have protected her has something else in mind. Without barely anything to her name she flees to escape the horrible fate into a land with a curse. You think that would worse not better but Caitlin with take the curse over the people she left behind in a heartbeat.<br /><br />I loved the Manor house and all of the oddities there. The mirrors were some of my favorite things as they seemed to hold so much magic. Some mirrors reflect you as you could be, or the house at a different time of day or they let you into the mind of someone from the past. Each mirror seemed special. Learning about the curse in the slow way information was given to the reader left me on edge wanting to know more and I was very surprised when the truth came to light. <br /><br />Caitlin and Anluan seemed like a natural fit and like most fairytales there isn’t much to the buildup of their relationship and I found I didn’t care. As soon as they start spending time on page together you can see where the relationship is going but I liked that Anluan wasn’t really a beast just gruff and marred by a palsy that made one side of his body weak. Caitlin saw the man underneath and strived to help him with the burdens of the Cursed Host he was in charge of and the upcoming threat from an army.<br /><br />Caitlin is the hero of the story for sure and almost everything is from her PoV. It made me feel like I was making the discoveries with her as the story progressed. I liked that she wasn’t a healer or just someone’s daughter but had an actual skill set to contribute to society. <br /><br />If you’ve enjoyed Mariller’s other tales this is on par with those in the feel, ton and pacing. <b>I think she is more for the patient reader that likes all the extra details and meandering down the path of the story in no hurry to get to the end.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16983442396631608536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I knew you could translate them, but...Caitrin, the idea of any action of mine causing you hurt is...it's unbearable. You are...you're like a beating heart. A glowing lamp. I've never met anyone like you before."</blockquote>

  <span id="freeText995467609941954705" style="display:none"><br><b>*3.5 stars* I think....</b><br><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Your coming here has changed everything, Caitrin. You have opened my mind to possibilities beyond any I had dreamed of. So I fetched the books. I knew you could translate them, but...Caitrin, the idea of any action of mine causing you hurt is...it's unbearable. You are...you're like a beating heart. A glowing lamp. I've never met anyone like you before."</blockquote>

So...yeah. Perhaps another weekend the story itself (and not just Anluan) would have captured my soul, but, as it is, the first 50% had a bit less Anluan than I would have liked, followed by a very, <i>very</i> good second half. I'm always so conflicted on how to rate these. <br><br><b>Mood vs story.<br>Male lead vs everything else<br>50/50 win/lose vs (again) my mood</b><br><br>So, yeah. I have no clue. The mystery as to who was a cruel, evil bastard of a villain was easy to spot from a mile away, but it didn't take anything away from the story, so that wasn't the problem. Perhaps her research? I don't know. Can't quite put my finger on it but...eh. <div id="review_129066162" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129066162" />
    <a title="new_user" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1365355-new-user"><img alt="new_user" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351189841p2/1365355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129066162?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="new_user" class="user" itemprop="url" name="new_user" href="/user/show/1365355-new-user">new_user</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Romance, Beauty and the Beast fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1365355-new-user?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129066162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6702003310901954224">Are you feeling nostalgic about your Beauty & the Beast days? I mean the Disney movie. Then you should totally read <i>Heart's Blood</i> by Juliet Marillier.<br/><br/>Her novels are as elegantly picked out as her pseudonym. Marillier's heroes and heroines are always so classy. They never say, "That bastard is a villain! Let's chop him in three!" They always maintain their humanity, and it isn't because they're too innocent to think of crueler alternatives. They're just above that, dude. <br/><br/>Her heroes and heroines h</span>
  <span id="freeText6702003310901954224" style="display:none">Are you feeling nostalgic about your Beauty &amp; the Beast days? I mean the Disney movie. Then you should totally read <i>Heart's Blood</i> by Juliet Marillier.<br /><br />Her novels are as elegantly picked out as her pseudonym. Marillier's heroes and heroines are always so classy. They never say, "That bastard is a villain! Let's chop him in three!" They always maintain their humanity, and it isn't because they're too innocent to think of crueler alternatives. They're just above that, dude. <br /><br />Her heroes and heroines have a purity to them, despite their mistakes, etc. Somehow, you know they always mean well. Is it because they only commit errors once it's well established that they are Good People? I don't think so.<br /><br />I loved Anluan. He's so brave and resilient. Even after all the bumps and bruises, he's still willing to get up if he sees hope-- which word was repeated much too often, by the way, LOL. Great secondary characters too. Just as endearing as Lumiere and Cogsworth, if less comedic, LOL.<br /><br />Marillier is so adept at evoking emotion. We truly feel the weariness and loneliness of leadership and the other burdens facing Anluan, where oddly one never sees this depicted except in passing.<br /><br />I loved the little similarities to B&amp;B, from the lonely cart trip and scary woods to the mirrors. This makes me want to watch the movie all over again.<br /><br />Of the books written in this theme, <i>Heart's Blood</i> is probably the most evocative of the emotion intended in the original that I've seen: the highs and lows, the terrible villainy/Fate, the beautiful heroics. She writes a fairy tale like nobody else. At the same time, the setting, characters, and plot are considerably different, so if you don't want to read a simple transcription of the movie, don't be worried. <br /><br />That said, I've seen Marillier plumb the depths of emotion more deeply, and her language and concepts -e.g. ancient lawmen- seemed much more simplistic here than her usual or adapted to a modern audience. I think she wanted to appeal to more readers.<br /><br />So this is not my favorite work from her but still a fabulous read! Even Marillier's lesser books are exceptional. Recommended for all B&amp;B fans or romance fans! (PG-13, but if I like it, you know it's not kiddy, LOL.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6702003310901954224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2314642364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2104104088340224511"><b>DNF ... 50 pages from the end</b><br/><br/>I'm sorry, but I just <i>can't do it</i> anymore. This is, quite simply, one of the <b>slowest</b> books I've ever read. Is it well written and atmospheric? Absolutely, yes. But I found neither the plot, nor the characters particularly compelling. <br/><br/>If I were being honest with myself, I'd recognise that I was trying to <b>force myself</b> to love this, simply because it's a <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> retelling. But there's no reason that I must love every single one ever written. After all, I wa</span>
  <span id="freeText2104104088340224511" style="display:none"><b>DNF ... 50 pages from the end</b><br /><br />I'm sorry, but I just <i>can't do it</i> anymore. This is, quite simply, one of the <b>slowest</b> books I've ever read. Is it well written and atmospheric? Absolutely, yes. But I found neither the plot, nor the characters particularly compelling. <br /><br />If I were being honest with myself, I'd recognise that I was trying to <b>force myself</b> to love this, simply because it's a <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> retelling. But there's no reason that I must love every single one ever written. After all, I was never too keen on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/544891.Beastly__Beastly___1__Kendra_Chronicles___1_" title="Beastly (Beastly, #1; Kendra Chronicles, #1) by Alex Flinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Beastly</a>. <br /><br />So, I'm parting ways with this book now. It's by no means a bad book, but it wasn't the one <b>for me</b>. I hope that others will enjoy it more than I have. <br /><br />For other <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> retellings or books influenced by the tale, I'd highly recommend:<br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839984.Cruel_Beauty" title="Cruel Beauty by Rosamund Hodge" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruel Beauty</a><br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a><br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40046030.Echo_North" title="Echo North by Joanna Ruth Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Echo North</a><br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24485589.Hunted" title="Hunted by Meagan Spooner" rel="nofollow noopener">Hunted</a><br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43204703.A_Curse_So_Dark_and_Lonely__Cursebreakers___1_" title="A Curse So Dark and Lonely (Cursebreakers, #1) by Brigid Kemmerer" rel="nofollow noopener">A Curse So Dark and Lonely</a></span>

<div id="review_400822176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/400822176" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/400822176?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=swoooon">swoooon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=rainy-day-re-reads">rainy-day-re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=beautiful-prose">beautiful-prose</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer400822176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1640952202022450365">Rating: 4.5 Stars <br/><br/>Although <i>Heart's Blood</i> is only my second Juliet Marillier novel, I can already count her amongst my favorite authors...ever. Marillier has a distinct style of writing stories about kind, but fierce, female protagonists and tortured romantic interests, creating beautiful love stories all against a backdrop of fantastical imagination. If that isn't a recipe for success, then I don't know what is. Yet, with <i>Heart's Blood</i>, Marillier has surpassed her previous prowess, writing one o</span>
  <span id="freeText1640952202022450365" style="display:none">Rating: 4.5 Stars <br /><br />Although <i>Heart's Blood</i> is only my second Juliet Marillier novel, I can already count her amongst my favorite authors...ever. Marillier has a distinct style of writing stories about kind, but fierce, female protagonists and tortured romantic interests, creating beautiful love stories all against a backdrop of fantastical imagination. If that isn't a recipe for success, then I don't know what is. Yet, with <i>Heart's Blood</i>, Marillier has surpassed her previous prowess, writing one of the most remarkable fairy tale re-telling of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> that I've ever come across. In fact, I'd go so far as to say that <i>Heart's Blood</i> has replaced <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> in my heart for I loved it far more than I did the original.<br /><br />Unlike many authors who allow the constrictions of a fairy tale re-telling to constrain their limits of creativity, <i>Heart's Blood</i> is based only loosely off of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>. Instead of brave Belle who replaces her father's place in the Beast's tower, we have strong Caitrin who seeks a job as a scribe on Whistling Tor, home to many mysteries. Instead of Beast, a truly horrific character, we have Anluan, a crippled and unhappy man who is oh-so-very-human. Instead of talking candles, clocks, and teapots, we have a motley crew of enigmatic spirits. And, most importantly perhaps, instead of a curse to correct the vanities of a foolish young prince, we have an age-old burden of evil and terror which is a curse like no other. While there are many similarities between the two tales, Marillier's takes on a life of its own quite often and the true linkage between these two fables is their combined theme of hope.<br /><br />Caitrin is a heroine I love. On the surface, she seems to be perfect: kind, gentle, fierce, and brave. Yet, as the novel progresses, we are able to slowly peel back the many layers to Caitrin's personality, revealing her insecurities, vulnerabilities, and flaws every bit as egregious as Anluan's. When we first meet Anluan - bitter, angry, and stubborn - it's hard to warm up to him, but before long, he becomes a love interest every bit as swoon-worthy as the next. Although <i>Heart's Blood</i> is, at its core, a novel about hope, it is also a romance and the slow, subtle, and skillfull manner in which Marillier brings together these two flawed beings is utter perfection. It will make you sigh with contentment for theirs is an epic tale that will worm its way firmly into your heart.<br /><br />In all honesty, there isn't very much more to say about <i>Heart's Blood</i>. Its realistic characters came alive for me, its intriguing setting grabbed me in from the first page, and the lore that this book is filled with is every bit as interesting as the fable it's based upon. If there are any faults to be found, they lie with the middle of the novel which became far too cheesy for my liking. Caitrin is the driving force behind Anluan's character change and much of that stems from the hope she gives him, but at times, this could borderline on preachy and become increasingly repetitive. Furthermore, the villain in this novel is rather obvious, but the multiple layers to the villain's evil nature will keep you on the edge of your seat, guessing until the end.<br /><br /><i>Heart's Blood</i> is, in so many ways, a perfect novel. Wonderfully flawed characters, atmospheric setting, and a romance that will make you crave for something that real yourself, it is a fairytale you won't want to leave. It has made me a die-hard Marillier fan and I will be rushing out to get my hands on all her other novels at once - this type of writing is just too good to wait for. It demands to be read, savored, and cherished like no other.<br /><br />You can read <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com/2012/10/review-hearts-blood-by-juliet-marillier.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on my blog, <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1640952202022450365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mellie Antoinette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mellie Antoinette" href="/user/show/47825764-mellie-antoinette">Mellie Antoinette</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1985429553821463386">“One hundred years of ill luck; one hundred years of sorrow; one hundred <br/> years of failure.”<br/><br/>All stories must begin somewhere. At the beginning. In the middle. In the “land beyond the gray.” They have shadows, souls, spirals and sentiment. And yet, they all have a small tie binding them together, the spirit of tales gone by, the luminescence of shadow black ink dripping from a feathered quill, the voice of the spoken word beating and beckoning to be heard.<br/><br/> “You came here with love in your heart. </span>
  <span id="freeText1985429553821463386" style="display:none">“One hundred years of ill luck; one hundred years of sorrow; one hundred <br /> years of failure.”<br /><br />All stories must begin somewhere. At the beginning. In the middle. In the “land beyond the gray.” They have shadows, souls, spirals and sentiment. And yet, they all have a small tie binding them together, the spirit of tales gone by, the luminescence of shadow black ink dripping from a feathered quill, the voice of the spoken word beating and beckoning to be heard.<br /><br /> “You came here with love in your heart. Perhaps it was the pattern of <br /> goodness that you brought with you. Perhaps it was the flowering of hope <br /> on the Tor.”<br /><br />This story begins where all good fairy tales tread - with a curse upon the enchanted castle of Whistling Tor and the ghostly inhabitants of its recesses and corners. It unfolds under the candlelight of a medieval library and burns in the beveled glass of a silver mirror. It is told in sorcerous spells of Latin and Irish to the few who can read, to the one who will listen. <br /><br /> “More than a year has passed since the day I first came up the hill to <br /> Whistling Tor and met a man with hair like fire and skin like snow.”<br /><br />Like this quote, it’s been many years since I’ve immersed myself in a well written Marillier. I had forgotten how well she builds her notes, melodies upon refrains, until the tone is so well matched, that the underlying song can only be beautiful and mellifluous (💃🏻yep, totally busted that one out of it’s hidey hole!). Yes, I’m a sucker for a Beauty and the Beast retelling, but do you know what really makes my heart race in romantic blushes and butterfly eyes? Good storytelling! And this one’s got it, in leaps and bounds! xoxo 💋</span>

Heart's Blood absolutely delivers on that count.<br/><br/>This book is in many ways standard Marillier fare: excellent prose; varied and multilayered characters; familiar yet intriguing magic; an exploration of the themes of friendship, family, and loyalty; and, of course, a slow burn romance. But standard for Marillier is also the mark of excellence, and however many time</span>
  <span id="freeText9235294667075897228" style="display:none">One of the things I love most about reading a book by Juliet Marillier is that I know going in I'm guaranteed a satisfying experience. Heart's Blood absolutely delivers on that count.<br /><br />This book is in many ways standard Marillier fare: excellent prose; varied and multilayered characters; familiar yet intriguing magic; an exploration of the themes of friendship, family, and loyalty; and, of course, a slow burn romance. But standard for Marillier is also the mark of excellence, and however many times she brings it to bear, it is never tiresome to read, and never fails to remind me that authors like her are what keep me reading.</span>

<div id="review_2702002845" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2702002845" />
    <a title="Charlotte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte"><img alt="Charlotte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487528389p2/11475773.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2702002845?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte">Charlotte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11475773-charlotte?shelf=trauma-rep">trauma-rep</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2702002845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17287245660894857270"><i>"But we’re not on our own anymore. We’re all here together, we’re all Lord Anluan’s people, the people of the Tor, and there’s enough strength in us to do the right things and make the right choices."</i><br/><br/>Heart's Blood is a 2009 historical fantasy work by Juliet Marillier. In all honesty this book made me so weepy that it'd be embarrassing if I wasn't totally determined to be completely unabashed about the feelings that this reading project inspires in me. NO SHAME 2019. (CW: discussion of physical a</span>
  <span id="freeText17287245660894857270" style="display:none"><i>"But we’re not on our own anymore. We’re all here together, we’re all Lord Anluan’s people, the people of the Tor, and there’s enough strength in us to do the right things and make the right choices."</i><br /><br />Heart's Blood is a 2009 historical fantasy work by Juliet Marillier. In all honesty this book made me so weepy that it'd be embarrassing if I wasn't totally determined to be completely unabashed about the feelings that this reading project inspires in me. NO SHAME 2019. (CW: discussion of physical and emotional abuse.)<br /><br /><b>So What's It About?</b><br /><br />This is a retelling of the classic fairy tale Beauty and the Beast set in Ireland during the time of the Norman invasions in the 12th century. Still grieving her beloved father's death, Caitrin flees the abuse of her stepmother and stepbrother and finds refuge in the remote, eerie town of Whistling Tor. She can't believe her luck when she is hired as a scribe up at the castle, but as she comes to know the castle's ghostly inhabitants and its mercurial lord Anluan, she becomes drawn into the story of their tragic pasts and finds herself in the middle of their struggle for a better future.<br /><br /><b>What I Thought</b><br /><br />This is, fundamentally, a book about overcoming the darkness of the past to create a more hopeful future by standing together and believing in the possibility of unity and change. Over the course of the book you slowly see hope take root in the lost souls of Whistling Tor, and it's a beautiful thing to behold. I think that is the lovely thing that is at the heart of Beauty and the Beast's magic: one live spark of a soul can infuse new life and joy in even the most desperate of crumbling ruins; even a Beast that has known nothing but despair for ages can come to see that he is capable of becoming more than he already is through the example set by the right Beauty.<br /><br />Caitrin is steadfast in the face of darkness, and that darkness lingers throughout the whole novel. Heart's Blood is oozing with Gothic sensibilities - chilling mysteries, dark passions, hidden secrets and forbidding ghosts lurking in the misty forest:<br /><br /><i>“Oh God, oh God!” someone screamed, as behind the rider a swirling mass flowed out from under the trees around the courtyard, not mist, not smoke, but something full of gaping mouths and clutching hands, something with a hundred shrieking, moaning voices and a hundred creeping, pattering feet.</i><br /><br />What I think is brilliant is that the horde is revealed to be monstrous only because they have come to believe themselves capable of nothing but monstrosity. Caitrin refuses to see them as anything less than her equals -individuals who are capable of both good and evil, and have control over their fates. She comes to know them individually, and they are delightful - a regretful commander, an unrepentant monk, a lost little girl, a steadfast soldier, all of whom have been trapped in an unending eternity of servitude:<br /><br /><i>Not creatures of ancient legend; not devils or demons. All the same, my skin prickled as I looked at them: here a woman carrying an injured child, there an old man with a heavy bag over his shoulder, his back bent, his limbs shaking; under an oak, a younger man whose fingers clutched feverishly onto an amulet strung around his neck. There were warriors and priests here, little girls and old women.</i><br /><br />Her firm belief in their capacity for goodness ends up being infectious, and they begin to stir out of the despair that has gripped them for centuries. They maintain their sanity when Anluan leaves the grounds of the castle, when in the past they have always rampaged! They unite with the villagers and defeat the Normans! And, finally, they experience the release from their curse that they have been awaiting for centuries, and depart the mortal world.<br /><br />At the same time that she gets to know the spirits of Whistling Tor, Caitrin begins the delicate process of getting to know the skittish and moody lord of the castle, Anluan. He is disfigured, disabled and mired in a sense of his own uselessness. Their relationship progresses slowly, with fits and starts and a gradual process of overcoming self-doubt and fear on both sides. This kind of hesitant romance between two uncertain lost souls is the type of romance that brings me the greatest joy. What's more, Anluan and Caitrain encourage each other to be braver and stronger people:<br /><br /><i>“You could practice being brave a little at a time.”<br />“What do you mean?”<br />“Choose a small fear, show yourself you can face it. Then a bigger one.”</i><br /><br />Isn't that what a good partnership is, when it comes down to it?<br /><br /><b>The F Word</b><br /><br />At this point my list of books to review has taken on a rather Sisyphian look, but the good news is that I've read enough to starting to notice patterns in the books I select. I think I'm going to be spending a lot of time talking about trauma here. I'm not going to turn this into Charlotte's Personal Issues Corner, but I'll just say that trauma is something that I already give a lot of consideration in my own life, and I'm glad to have the opportunity to talk about it in terms of literature here. I've decided to discuss all trauma-related considerations in "The F Word" section of my review because I consider the accurate, thought-provoking examination of female trauma a feminist act, and depictions of female characters surviving, coping and accessing personal power in the face of traumatic experiences are extremely important to me.<br /><br />With that being said, Caitrin flees a horribly abusive home at the beginning of the novel, and she is marked by her history throughout the story. She criticizes herself with the same horrible words that were used against her and sometimes succumbs to self-blame and considers herself a coward and weakling for "allowing" herself to be abused and staying in the situation as long as she did:<br /><br /><i>"...the worst thing wasn’t Cillian’s fists or Ita’s cruel tongue. It was me. It was the way the two of them turned me into a helpless child, full of self-loathing and timidity."</i><br /><br />Her story shows the immense difficulty that many women have in leaving abusive homes, and the incredible danger inherent to that process. Her time at Whistling Tor helps her heal, and grow in self-confidence to the extent that she is finally able to face her abusers and reclaim what they stole from her. What I especially appreciated about this confrontation was that Caitrin does not try to face them by herself but is surrounded by people who care about her and have her back when she returns to her old home.<br /><br />Another thing that I really appreciated about Heart's Blood from a feminist perspective is its refreshing portrayal of lust. Caitrin's desire for Anluan is so forthright and free of shame without seeming forced or over-exaggerated in any way. When they do sleep together, I think Marillier describes the scene with a really mature and touching sense of what sex is actually like for real people, especially given Anluan's sense of self-doubt and insecurity about his disfigurement/disability:<br /><br /><i>"This had been real: real in its flaws and uncertainties, real in its small triumphs, real in its compromises and understanding."</i><br /><br />The book also has some sympathy for its villainess, and I was certainly left with the impression that the ultimate villainy was the way that Muirne had been groomed into her evil ways and then promptly used in the most horrible manner and disposed of by Anluan's great-grandfather. In addition to Muirne's acts of deception and cruelty, Caitrin reflects that ultimately she still has "the voice of a girl just come to womanhood, a voice of longing, yearning, promise: Look at me. See me. Love me."<br /><br />In the end, Heart's Blood argues that that is what we all deserve.<br /><br /><b>About the Author</b><br /><br />Born in New Zealand in 1948, Juliet Marillier was educated at the University of Otago with a BA in languages and a Bachelors in Music. She worked as a high school and university level music teacher, an opera singer and choral conductor before becoming an author full time. She is an active writing mentor, gives many writing workshops and remains active in her local writing community. She is a member of The Order of Bards, Ovates and Druids and lives with a "pack" of rescue dogs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17287245660894857270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
