<div id="review_1638313338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1638313338" />
    <a title="Kaila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35924884-kaila"><img alt="Kaila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533304308p2/35924884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1638313338?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaila" href="/user/show/35924884-kaila">Kaila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405039437" href="/book/show/7177275-heart-s-blood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=beautiful-writing">beautiful-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=angels-and-demons">angels-and-demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=slow-burn">slow-burn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=best-heroines">best-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=beauty-and-the-beast-esque">beauty-and-the-beast-esque</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=with-children">with-children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638313338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12977531014189438855"><b>4.5/5 stars</b> <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>“Even in that time of utter darkness, somewhere deep inside me the memory of love and goodness had stayed alive.” </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This was a fantastic book, but I wasn't expecting anything less from this author. Anyone who knows me knows that I love all things <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> related. So, I was <b>beyond excited </b>when I found one of my favourite authors has written a retelling of my favourite gothic tale. This is by far <b>the best <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> retelling </b>as it took this old story and trans</span>
  <span id="freeText12977531014189438855" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5 stars</b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Even in that time of utter darkness, somewhere deep inside me the memory of love and goodness had stayed alive.” </b>
</blockquote><br><br>This was a fantastic book, but I wasn't expecting anything less from this author. Anyone who knows me knows that I love all things <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> related. So, I was <b>beyond excited </b>when I found one of my favourite authors has written a retelling of my favourite gothic tale. This is by far <b>the best <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> retelling </b>as it took this old story and transformed it into something new and unique. This book was full of dark secrets, mystery, romance, hope and friendship. The cast of characters had this amazing chemistry together, and I loved each of them for a different reason. Once again, like with all of <i>Juliet Marillier's</i> books, it was <b>phenomenally written </b>and <b>absolutely captivating</b>. I loved this book, even if it wasn't as good as <i>Daughter of the Forest.</i><br><br>Like always, I am at a loss for words when trying to describe a Juliet Marillier book. It was very complex and unique, unlike any <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> retelling that I've read before. I'm going to try and simplify the synopsis, but just trust me when I say, it is better than anything that I can describe or write about.<br><br>Caitrin has been an orphan ever since her father died, and has been forced to live with extended family that have taken advantage of her situation, she has finally gathered the courage to run away and her money seems to take her as far as Whistling Tor. This town is unlike any that Caitrin has visited before, full of whispers, mystery and superstition. The people of the town whisper most about the old fortress above the hill, and the crippled chieftain that lives within it. Anluan, the chieftain, is spoken of horribly throughout Tor, as his family has been cursed for generations. But this crumbling fortress becomes a sort of safe haven for Caitrin, as she works as a scribe for the mysterious chieftain. Despite the warnings that people gave her and the quick temper of Anluan, Caitrin tries her best to think compassionately about this strange place, and the even stranger people who live there.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"You are...you're like a beating heart. A glowing lamp. I've never met anyone like you before."</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Juliet Marillier has taken a classic love story and really flipped it on its head. I don't know how many times I can say how unique this book is compared to other retellings, so just believe me already. This story <b>constantly surprised me</b> and took the plot in directions that I never would have imagined. I was in awe by the <b>imaginative beauty</b> of this book and the flawless storytelling that intertwined an original story with one of my favourite classics. No, there is no beast in this book but there is a crippled man who sees himself as a monster. No, the fortress' library is not the most grand you've ever seen, but it is enough for the young scribe Caitrin. No, there are no dancing and singing furniture, but you should definitely beware of the mirrors that seem to tell tales of a different time. As you can see, <i>Heart's Blood</i> uses the original classic as a mere guideline as the author transports you through a breathtaking, whimsical and mysterious tale.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488631589ra/22137879.gif" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The characters in this book were <b>deeply intriguing</b>. Whistling Tor was a very strange place, and with it came some strange people, but I loved them all. Every character was three-dimensional and complex. Each chapter we learnt more about this cast of characters, as their personalities were slowly revealed to us. This book had a big focus on a person's history and the idea of redemption, which played a part in the intricacies of many of these characters. They were not perfect, and the author acknowledged this. In particular, I adored Caitrin. She was such a strong heroine, but in the less conventional ways. She was hopeful, kind, intelligent and curious. She wasn't perfect though, instead her vulnerabilities and flaws just made her more loveable. She was just such a <i>real</i> heroine and someone that I could strongly connect to.<br><br>The setting of this novel was definitely one of my favourite aspects. It was just so atmospheric, and contributed to every part of the story. I was immediately drawn in by the mysterious nature of Whistling Tor, which never fully revealed itself to me. It was this <b>constant source of intrigue</b> in the storyline the setting was dynamic, and seemed to change along with the characters. Marillier wrote the setting to be rich in history, personality and mystery; much like the characters in the story. I especially loved the setting because it brought a very gothic undertone to the story. This gothic nature of the book really ties this retelling to the original story.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“This had been real: real in its flaws and uncertainties, real in its small triumphs, real in its compromises and understanding.” </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I think in every review I've written about a Juliet Marillier book, I've gushed about her beautiful writing style. She is definitely one of my favourite authors, and I've only read four of her books so far. She has such a talent for storytelling and <b>poetic, gorgeous writing. </b>Every word she writes is purposeful, and I gobble them up <b>like an addict!</b><br><br>Even though I loved this book, I didn't enjoy it as much as <i>Daughter of the Forest.</i> Part of this may be because I read it on a midnight flight and I was super tired. Other than that, I don't really know what is making me give this a four star rating rather than a five. I do think it was a little slow at the start, but other than that, it's just an overall unexplainable feeling I have. Perhaps it's just because I loved her other books so much that I had unbelievably high expectations for this one.<br><br>I also loved the romance in this novel. Of course, it is a retelling of an old romantic tale, of the romance played a large role in the story. Anluan and Caitlin's relationship was a quietly powerful presence in the book. It was not an in-your-face kind of love, but it subtly took root and began to grow and intertwine with the branches of the story. I felt the connection very deeply as their relationship seemed pure, mature and based on a strong friendship. So basically, it's safe to say that<b> I loved the relationship</b> and both of our main characters.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“He was sitting not far away, watching me, and I surprised a smile on his face, the first real smile I had ever seen him give, a smile that curved and softened the tight mouth, and warmed the ice-cool eyes; a smile that brought the blood to my face and made my heart turn over.”</b>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="12977531014189438855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2266278366" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2266278366" />
    <a title="Deborah Ideiosepius" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius"><img alt="Deborah Ideiosepius" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425943228p2/4802663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2266278366?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Ideiosepius" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Ideiosepius" href="/user/show/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius">Deborah Ideiosepius</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405039437" href="/book/show/7177275-heart-s-blood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius?shelf=2019-reading-challenge">2019-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius?shelf=wordpress">wordpress</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius?shelf=australian-authors">australian-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius?shelf=historic-fiction">historic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius?shelf=magic-realism">magic-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2266278366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5391061105119434390">This was a rich, complex reading experience. If reading were a fabric, this would have been yards and yards of soft velvet, all colours, folded and scrunched, smooth ans sleek.<br/><br/>On the run from a nightmarish family situation Caitrin is desperately hoping to find a place where she can make her way as a scribe, her father trained her up to be one of the best and it is all she knows. It is a precarious chance though, because women scribes are not acknowledged in this patriarchal society of.... Ah yes</span>
  <span id="freeText5391061105119434390" style="display:none">This was a rich, complex reading experience. If reading were a fabric, this would have been yards and yards of soft velvet, all colours, folded and scrunched, smooth ans sleek.<br /><br />On the run from a nightmarish family situation Caitrin is desperately hoping to find a place where she can make her way as a scribe, her father trained her up to be one of the best and it is all she knows. It is a precarious chance though, because women scribes are not acknowledged in this patriarchal society of.... Ah yes, what exactly is this society? The social structure seems to be that of Ireland, 9th century-ish, to my untutored eyes, but the Normans are invading, so that would be more 13th? Anyway, it is a romatiscised historical Ireland, only with magic, curses and wraiths added in to the mix. Lovely world building, done with a gentle yet deft touch, we don't need to know too much about it for the story to work and we are given no more than we need.<br /><br />In her head long flight from her past, (no spoilers, the slow reveal within the pages is perfect) Caitrin has just reached the end of her funds. The cart she was traveling on put her down on a deserted, darkening road and she has few choices as to where to look for shelter. The isolated village of Whistling Tor takes her in for the night, the next day she finds that the chieftain on the hill needs a scribe and against all warnings goes for it.<br /><br />The household is irregular and eerie, the job fascinating and overwhelming, the Lord, Anluan occupies more and more of Caitrin's attention as through her reading and transcribing she learns more and more about the curse that lies of his household, and the wraiths which swarm the hill.<br /><br />This book absolutely exceeded expectation, and I had pretty high expectations. The writing is beautiful, one feels like time is suspended while you are reading it, so successfully does it pull you into the story, the outside world receding while you read. Caitlin is a part of that, but while she is the central character and the main focus of the story, a believable, likable, well written young woman she does not need to carry the story alone. The actual plot is subtle with hidden depths, it unravels slowly and as it undulates its way through the 400 odd pages, charming you as you go.<br /><br />While this book is described as being 'inspired' by beauty and the beast, I am not sure I would have picked up on that if the cover had not told me. There are many elements that fit, of course; the characters, plot, world building, these all are very much 'fairy tale' motifs. Lorn Anluan, under a strange curse, with irregular house staff and a library full of secrets... yes, I can see that similarity. The magical reading experience with its lush feel, even in the bleak bits - that is very much what one expects from a fairy tale.<br /><br />However, I think it is much more a 'modern' fairy tale than a re-telling of beauty on the beast because all the distinct plot elements that are present in that fairy tail are modified and more complicated in Heart;s Blood. A fair tail has to be basic, almost to a instinctive level and this novel is too rich to be stereotypical. The lord does not take Caitrin captive, he offers her a paid contract. He never did anything to be cursed for and his physical appearance is due to a childhood incident. Caitrin solves the curse, but not by anything a wimpy as a kiss, rather through research, guts, perseverance and intelligence. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ But, if we do accept it as a re-telling of beauty and the beast, then how good is it, to finally have a 'beast' who does not change his appearance? Instead of the outmoded notion of the princess having to wed a 'handsome' prince, in this story the lead female is allowed to accept Lord Anluan's physical deformity for what it is, love the man anyway and accept him as he is! Anluan is also permitted to grow as a character, find his strength as a leader and a chieftain while still having a physical deformity. He is allowed to grow as a character without becoming stereotypically good looking or heroic Am I the only one who is massively excited by this I wonder? In the animated Beauty and the Beast I was that person, who saw the beast change into the 'handsome prince' and thought 'damn, I liked him better before'. There has, for me, always been a vague feeling of disquiet over the notion of the 'appearance curse' in fairy stories, even Shrek did it, though in reverse; did Fiona <i>want</i> to be a troll? No, not really, why was an appearance change always necessary for these kinds of tales?*ahem, steps off soapbox* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There was a lot to enjoy about the book while reading it, because while it was a slow reveal with lots of small events leading toward the conclusion, there was a lot to think over while one was not reading. Thoroughly recommend reading this lovely story.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5391061105119434390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1959452256" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1959452256" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1959452256?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1959452256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6739740838605508047">Caitrin, a young woman who trained with her father as a scribe, has come to Whistling Tor fleeing kinsman who have abused her. The Tor is a supernatural place peopled by uncanny forces and their strange chieftain Anluan. But Caitrin is far less scared of revenants, gigantic dogs and walking scarecrows than she is of who pursues her, so the Tor becomes a much needed home. Anluan is in need of a scribe for the summer so the arrangement works for both parties, but Caitrin quickly becomes fascinated</span>
  <span id="freeText6739740838605508047" style="display:none">Caitrin, a young woman who trained with her father as a scribe, has come to Whistling Tor fleeing kinsman who have abused her. The Tor is a supernatural place peopled by uncanny forces and their strange chieftain Anluan. But Caitrin is far less scared of revenants, gigantic dogs and walking scarecrows than she is of who pursues her, so the Tor becomes a much needed home. Anluan is in need of a scribe for the summer so the arrangement works for both parties, but Caitrin quickly becomes fascinated by the people of Whistling Tor, its mysteries and its lord.<br /><br />I've seen this referred to as a retelling of Beauty and the Beast, and there's certainly an element of that, but most of the key markers of that tale are absent here. Caitrin has come to the Tor looking for a refuge and a position; she wants to be there and at no point in the story does she want to leave. Anluan's "beastly" elements are a result of illness and depression: there's no physical transformation here. There is however a curse affecting the Tor and its people so that element does come through, and Caitrin's nature is that of a transforming beauty as well.<br /><br />In other respects, I found this is very similar to this author's Blackthorn and Grimm books with a supernatural mystery in an almost-historical ancient Ireland with an absolute loving attention to detail and atmosphere. Maybe not quite as polished as the later books, but still excellent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6739740838605508047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_569157128" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/569157128" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365166675p2/13954899.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/569157128?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8139058-heart-s-blood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=series-opener">series-opener</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=beauty-beast">beauty-beast</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=fantastical-romance">fantastical-romance</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer569157128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14758159078835713055">3.5 stars. Despite some pacing problems, Marillier spins a captivating yarn in <i>
  <b>Heart's Blood,</b>
</i> set in Ireland in the 12th Century, when Anglo-Normans invaded. Content includes one sex scene (not graphic, this is YA), dark sorcery, mutilation, battery, murder, etc.<br/><br/>Some say this is similar to <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>, but the supposed "Beast" (Lord Anluan) is not all <i>that </i>ugly. Nor is "Beauty" forced to live with him. She arrives voluntarily, seeking a job and safe refuge. The similarity rests in t</span>
  <span id="freeText14758159078835713055" style="display:none">3.5 stars. Despite some pacing problems, Marillier spins a captivating yarn in <i>
  <b>Heart's Blood,</b>
</i> set in Ireland in the 12th Century, when Anglo-Normans invaded. Content includes one sex scene (not graphic, this is YA), dark sorcery, mutilation, battery, murder, etc.<br /><br />Some say this is similar to <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>, but the supposed "Beast" (Lord Anluan) is not all <i>that </i>ugly. Nor is "Beauty" forced to live with him. She arrives voluntarily, seeking a job and safe refuge. The similarity rests in the fact that Whistling Tor is under a curse. Rather nicely done, too, the various manifestations of the dark enchantment.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Heart's Blood</b>
</i> is told in first person through Caitrin's POV, an 18-year-old orphan. Like her father, Caitrin is a scribe, able to read and write Latin and Irish. With dear papa now dead, she's on the run from greedy and abusive kinfolk. Her courage has taken a severe beating along with her shapely "whore's body" when that desperate flight from the village of Market Cross culminates at the very threshold of Whistling Tor, a cursed place:<blockquote>My vow to be brave made me straighten up and face the fortification. Four or five men stood on the other side, their faces uniformly ash-white, their weapons at the ready: a pitchfork, a scythe, an iron bar, a club with spikes. ‘Away with you, scum!’ yelled one, and another added, ‘Go back where you belong, into the pit of hell!’</blockquote><br /><br />We go from there, into the fantastical, with magical mirrors, the dark arts, an undead horse, a humongous hound, and hundreds of manifestations -- a "host" of spirits in limbo, forced to serve the Chieftain, Lord Anluan.<br /><br />Caitrin, kind at heart, takes pity on the restless phantasms and works against the clock to translate old Latin notebooks, seeking a way to break the curse and free the host. <br /><br />Meanwhile, she gradually falls in love with Anluan, helping this 25-year-old chieftain overcome apathy, even despair. He's not a man of optimism. Since birth, life has been hard, with beloved parents dying in tragic circumstances, childhood palsy weakening his muscles and disfiguring his face, and every day, the constant need to control his vile inheritance: Keeping peace within his army of ghouls is mentally exhausting. <br /><br />Caitrin -- hands down the main protagonist -- also forms wonderful friendships with his loyal retainers (Mangus, Olcan and Fianchu, Rioghan, Eichri) and some other characters, like Tomas, Orna, Gearrog, Cathair, and the little girl. (I enjoyed these secondary characters). <br /><br />No spoilers, but some parts are quite gripping. I enjoyed it. I cannot decide if I liked it more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/441689827" rel="nofollow noopener"> Daughter of the Forest</a> or not. Nah.<br /><br /><b>WHY ONLY THREE STARS?</b><br /><br />1) From the beginning I determined the identity of the villain. It's very obvious, so no suspense, except wondering when our heroine will figure it out. (And no way would it take Caitrin <i>that long</i> to get a clue.)<br /><br />2) The pacing drags a little at times. I thought about skimming ahead. <br /><br />3) I did not feel drawn deeply into the relationship between Caitrin and Anluan. They didn't talk all that much. <br /><br />4) The theme is HOPE. Don't give up hope. Dare to hope. Hope when all seems lost. I repeat myself? So does the author. (It gets tiresome, actually.)<br /><br />PS. Another theme is COURAGE. Find enough courage to take the next small step. This message is clear, too, but not overdone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14758159078835713055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3223360128" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3223360128" />
    <a title="Allison Hurd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14495279-allison-hurd"><img alt="Allison Hurd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530670583p2/14495279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3223360128?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison Hurd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison Hurd" href="/user/show/14495279-allison-hurd">Allison Hurd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=fem-author">fem-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3223360128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10518071900006849704">Okay, listen. Not everything has to be insta-classic, you know? Even my bitter heart sometimes just wants the nice people to put their faces together until babies pop out (I'm from an abstinence-only county, so I think this is how it works) and this is it. Juliet gets the parts of the romance that are heart-warming, without really focusing overly on the sex, which is nice. After the testosterone-filled book I just finished, the estrogen-filled one is a nice counterpoint.<br/><br/><b>CONTENT WARNING</b>: <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view sp</a></span>
  <span id="freeText10518071900006849704" style="display:none">Okay, listen. Not everything has to be insta-classic, you know? Even my bitter heart sometimes just wants the nice people to put their faces together until babies pop out (I'm from an abstinence-only county, so I think this is how it works) and this is it. Juliet gets the parts of the romance that are heart-warming, without really focusing overly on the sex, which is nice. After the testosterone-filled book I just finished, the estrogen-filled one is a nice counterpoint.<br /><br /><b>CONTENT WARNING</b>: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ domestic violence, suicide, loss of a parent, neglect of a child, house fire, death of a dog.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><u>Things to love:</u><br /><br />-<b>It's so sweet</b>. Like the movie "Ghost," but with illuminated script instead of pottery.<br /><br />-<b>The premise</b>. Ooo a good Irish ghost story!<br /><br />-<b>Happy ever after</b>. It's not that deep, just let it be happy.<br /><br />-<b>What a girl wants/needs</b>. What I love most about Juliet's romances is that they're soooo actually unromantic for the most part. It's full of big strong men who dote on the little lady and who tell her she's beautiful even if she's not [insert whatever beauty means in the heroine's eyes] and they just love love love strong women who win their hearts and sway their minds and teach them peace. Yeah! <i>Yeah</i>! Love your strong women, male characters! Be in awe, but also, like, be totally cool to call down fire and brimstone on people who would harm them, because who doesn't like to think about strong arms and sly smiles or whatever?<br /><br />Ahem.<br /><br />-<b>The right way to transcribe books</b>. What <i> The Twisted Ones </i> did wrong, this gets right. Horror, magic, despair--just great.<br /><br />-<b>The end</b>. It's just such a pretty bow!<br /><br /><u>Things that were not top shelf:</u><br /><br />-<b>The mystery</b>. Lol. What do you like about Juliet's books you ask me? Strong heroines. The mythology. Historical fiction. You will notice that absent on that list is her ability to tell a mystery. She just can't do it, gods love her. It's not about the mystery, even if it is a mystery, okay? It's about the hair tumbling from somewhere to someplace else, and the love shining in eyes the color of [some primal thing that everybody admires.] <br /><br />-<b>It is what it is</b>. This is every "shy girl becomes queen" story. It is what it is. It's not more than that.<br /><br />-<b>A bit blunt</b>. What I love about her first series is the slow burn, and the believable path to something wonderful. We wipe all that off the table here. <br /><br />3.5 stars rounded up because the world is a cesspool and I'm glad to find some magic in it, even if it's smoochy magic.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10518071900006849704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16957815378633972256" style="display:none">DNF at 53%.<br /><br />A well-intentioned but dreadfully boring story. I suspect Juliet Marillier and I are just not meant to be, which is truly tragic as there aren't that many authors around capable of writing both fascinating fantasy worlds and strong romantic narratives, a type of story I can't get enough of. But her heroines always have the mark of the <s>Beast</s> Mary Sue, and that's one of the biggest bookish turn off for me. Also, while I don't particularly mind lengthy descriptions, the 250+ pages I've read alone are in dire need of a good trimming down, if nothing else because hitting your readers over their heads with fairly simple concepts and info about the worldbuilding isn't particularly flattering and they might suspect, like I did, that the author believes them to be a bunch of idiots.</span>

<div id="review_175646902" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/175646902" />
    <a title="Kay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5611008-kay"><img alt="Kay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314169555p2/5611008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/175646902?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kay" href="/user/show/5611008-kay">Kay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451463265" href="/book/show/7938503-heart-s-blood">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Beauty and the Beast...without the hints of bestiality</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5611008-kay?shelf=once-upon-a-time">once-upon-a-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5611008-kay?shelf=quite-the-romantic">quite-the-romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5611008-kay?shelf=life-after-death">life-after-death</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175646902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11775367651816532552">This was a lovely book. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier' title='Juliet Marillier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Juliet Marillier</a>, how do you do it? How do you write about such beautifully scarred individuals learning to find courage, play my heart strings like a harp, and create such a unique, sincere rendition without unnecessary melodrama and violence?<br/><br/>This is quite possibly one of the best renditions of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> I've read or seen (though the Disney version holds a special place in my heart, yes, even with the talking silverware). <br/><br/>I think the core element of <i>Beauty and</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11775367651816532552" style="display:none">This was a lovely book. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier" title="Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Juliet Marillier</a>, how do you do it? How do you write about such beautifully scarred individuals learning to find courage, play my heart strings like a harp, and create such a unique, sincere rendition without unnecessary melodrama and violence?<br /><br />This is quite possibly one of the best renditions of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> I've read or seen (though the Disney version holds a special place in my heart, yes, even with the talking silverware). <br /><br />I think the core element of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> is about love between two individuals, a love that overcomes emotional differences and physical appearance. It's about trust, sacrifice, and devotion. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6278019.Heart_s_Blood__Whistling_Tor___1_" title="Heart's Blood (Whistling Tor, #1) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Heart's Blood</a> has this in spades, and more. What I loved about this rendition is that Anluan [the Beast] was not the only one who was terribly scarred--Caitrin [the Beauty] was as well. I really enjoyed reading about how the two overcame their fears by borrowing courage from one another, and coming to terms with the horrors of their past.<br /><br />The atmospheric quality of this novel was very unique to other Marillier books I've read. Set in a crumbling castle haunted by ghosts and a suspcious housekeeper that reminded me of Mrs. Danvers from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12873.Rebecca" title="Rebecca by Daphne du Maurier" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebecca</a>, the book has a decidedly gothic feel, in all its creepiness and black-veiled romance. All of the elements of the original fairy tale were also there, from the flowers, the curse, the enchanted mirrors--though with a decidedly Marillieresque twist. <br /><br />The only issue I had that prevented the fifth star was that the antagonist was immediately apparent, and at times it frustrated me that no one else saw this coming from a mile away. <br /><br />But still, the point of this novel wasn't to find the culprit (well, maybe just a little). This novel is worth reading for its beautiful romance and its lightening messages of finding hope through courage.<br /><br /><b>4 STARS AND HIGHLY RECOMMENDED</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11775367651816532552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828590-eric?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828590-eric?shelf=folk-tales">folk-tales</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2318975765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7814782000865404404">4.5 stars<br/><br/><i>Heart's Blood</i> is a surprisingly entertaining and satisfying fantasy read. I read this book as a buddy read with my friends in the Bookish Buddies book club. Another great choice!<br/><br/>When I embarked on reading this book, I had the impression that it was sort of retelling of the original <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>. I don't recall reading the original story. <i> Heart's Blood</i>, for me, bore very little resemblance to the more popular versions (ala Disney) of B&B. There are no talking tea cups in this st</span>
  <span id="freeText7814782000865404404" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br /><i>Heart's Blood</i> is a surprisingly entertaining and satisfying fantasy read. I read this book as a buddy read with my friends in the Bookish Buddies book club. Another great choice!<br /><br />When I embarked on reading this book, I had the impression that it was sort of retelling of the original <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>. I don't recall reading the original story. <i> Heart's Blood</i>, for me, bore very little resemblance to the more popular versions (ala Disney) of B&amp;B. There are no talking tea cups in this story. <br /><br />The story starts with Caitrin running away from her home town. She's a young woman who happens to be a professional scribe. A respectable craft that she learned from her father who had died suddenly. Caitrin finds herself in a weird land where there are "voices" in the forest full of ghosts. It so happens there is a scribe's job at the chieftain's manor. Caitrin is broke so decides she is going to inquire about the job. To get to the manor though, she has to travel through the haunted forest. She manages to get through the forest to meet the main caretaker, the kindly Mangus. She also meets the chieftain Anluan. Anluan, it turns out, to be a young man who has a disability. The are other strange people about the manor as well. Caitrin gets the job even though the people don't expect her to stay long. No one ever does.<br /><br />The writing has a fluidity to it that kept me hooked into the story. The characters are well developed and there are a lot of interesting story elements. The storytelling has a traditional feel and indeed a good part of the story is about hope, love, loyalty, good, evil and life lessons. I liked that story gets down to the person level of the characters. Also, sort of neatly tucked into the plot is a mystery and the search for clues. Parts of the story has horror elements to it while other parts are quite heartwarming. Finally, this story is written for adults and perhaps older teens.<br /><br />This story surprised me as being good fantasy with kind of traditional fairy tale feel. The author calls it "historical fantasy." Whatever the story style is called, it worked for me. I'll plan to explore more works by this author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7814782000865404404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1323940762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1323940762" />
    <a title=" Simply Sam ツ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14235956-simply-sam"><img alt=" Simply Sam ツ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468513067p2/14235956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1323940762?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Simply Sam ツ" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Simply Sam ツ" href="/user/show/14235956-simply-sam"> Simply Sam ツ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14235956-simply-sam?shelf=fairy-tale-feel">fairy-tale-feel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14235956-simply-sam?shelf=re-tellings">re-tellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14235956-simply-sam?shelf=fantasy-romance">fantasy-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1323940762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1999948339188029175">I’ve loved Juliet Marillier since reading Daughter of the Forest. She’s one of my bucket list authors that I hope to read, or at least attempt to read, all of her works. She has such an amazing way with weaving a tale, of creating emotions and atmosphere. Her books all feel a little bit like magic. I seriously love her style. So, when I discovered that she had written a re-telling of Beauty and the Beast it immediately went on my TBR list. Unfortunately, I have way too many books on that list wi</span>
  <span id="freeText1999948339188029175" style="display:none">I’ve loved Juliet Marillier since reading Daughter of the Forest. She’s one of my bucket list authors that I hope to read, or at least attempt to read, all of her works. She has such an amazing way with weaving a tale, of creating emotions and atmosphere. Her books all feel a little bit like magic. I seriously love her style. So, when I discovered that she had written a re-telling of Beauty and the Beast it immediately went on my TBR list. Unfortunately, I have way too many books on that list with not enough time to read them (book reader problems, am I right?) so it waited patiently for 2+ years for me to get around to it. This past weekend, we had no plans so it was the perfect opportunity to cozy up to a book and spend the weekend reading.<br /><br /><i>“But hope is such a tenuous quality. To feel it and then to be denied what one most longs for…Better, surely, not to hope at all, than to open the heart to a hope that is impossible.”</i><br /><br />Heart’s Blood maintains the feeling of what I consider the classic telling of Beauty and the Beast, having derelict castle whose curse encompasses all those who live within its borders, including its “beastly” master. But as with all her works, Mrs. Marillier was able to add her own spin to the story. Caitrin, our young protagonist, is the on the run from her wicked aunt and cousin. After the death of her father, the two of them swooped in like greedy vultures and claimed inheritance to the estate. Lost in her own grief, Caitrin was in no position to defend herself against them. She suffered at their hands, both mentally and physically, for nearly a year before she finds the courage to get away. Her escape led her to Whistling Tor, with a village surrounded by a formidable barrier, with tales of a forest filled with whispers and manifestations, and with a warped and twisted chieftain who ruled over it all. Despite the warnings from the villagers, Caitrin gains employment as a scribe at the castle, home to an interesting array of characters, from the gnome-like Olcan and his giant dog Fianchu, to the austere lady but not quite Lady Muirne, to the bickering Rioghan and Brother Eichri, and at the heart of it all, Lord Anluan, the misshapen master. It doesn’t take long for Caitrin to realize there is more to the story than just superstitious gossip and as she grows closer to this family of oddities, she knows that she must do everything in her power to help them. <br /> <br /><i>“Patterns could be broken; paths could be changed. All it took was courage.”</i><br /><br />And hope. That’s really what this story is about. It’s the hope that we can control our futures, that there is, even in the darkest of times, a way back into the light. <br /><br />I loved the supporting cast, including the host. Give me a good, haunted, creepy forest any day. I also really like the way the relationship between the castle inhabitants and the village was handled in the end, that they come together to fight a common enemy versus becoming the enemy to one another. <br /><br />I think there were a few things that she left open, such as Olcan and his back-story (which hints at a fae ancestry though it is never expounded upon) as well as the history of the mirrors, which could have been explained a little more fully. Especially the mirrors. What’s the origin? Did Nechtan really create them all? And to what purpose? And one mirror is a little different from the rest. Why? <br />I also found the Anluan sending Caitrin away a little messy. If he really wanted her to leave and believe he did not want her, why send what he did with her? It doesn’t make sense. Also, the real reason for it seemed a little bit immature. It just didn’t quite click for me. Also, the “bad guy” reveal was definitely no shocker. I knew almost from the onset who it was. <br /><br />However, I don’t read her works to be shocked, I read her works to be swept up in the characters stories and their emotions. Did she deliver here? Yes and no. I felt a little ambivalent when it came to Anluan and Caitrin. Don’t get me wrong, I always want the beast to end up with the beauty (or to end up with another beast, so long as he’s happy), but I found them both to be a little bit boring. I liked them well enough, they just weren’t supremely interesting. <br /><br />So where does that leave me? I loved the setting, the atmosphere, and the secondary characters. I liked the story well enough, though the two main characters were a little on the boring side. I’m not disappointed, per se, but I do think there was something lacking. I’m giving it 3.5 stars, but I’m rounding it up to 4.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1999948339188029175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10560917630479852984" style="display:none">This book made me fall in love all over again with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8649.Juliet_Marillier" title="Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Juliet Marillier</a>'s books after I DNF ed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13923.Blade_of_Fortriu__The_Bridei_Chronicles___2_" title="Blade of Fortriu (The Bridei Chronicles, #2) by Juliet Marillier" rel="nofollow noopener">Blade of Fortriu</a>. <div id="review_79898823" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79898823" />
    <a title="Erotic Horizon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1431636-erotic-horizon"><img alt="Erotic Horizon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1218892554p2/1431636.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79898823?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erotic Horizon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erotic Horizon" href="/user/show/1431636-erotic-horizon">Erotic Horizon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79898823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer390621843099406708">Every now and again I read a book that is simply perfection – Juliet Marillier – HEART’S BLOOD is one of those books for me. Prior to the release I remember seeing the cover and thought this book will knock my socks off and so said, so done.<br/><br/>The book starts of with Caitrin a young scribe making her way to parts unknown, running away from a greater evil. With only the bare minimum plus the tools of her trade as comfort, she is dropped off late in the evening in the woods near to what is known as W</span>
  <span id="freeText390621843099406708" style="display:none">Every now and again I read a book that is simply perfection – Juliet Marillier – HEART’S BLOOD is one of those books for me. Prior to the release I remember seeing the cover and thought this book will knock my socks off and so said, so done.<br /><br />The book starts of with Caitrin a young scribe making her way to parts unknown, running away from a greater evil. With only the bare minimum plus the tools of her trade as comfort, she is dropped off late in the evening in the woods near to what is known as Whistling Tor. <br /><br />Not only is Caitrin cold and frightened but she is determined to move on because what is behind her is far worse than what is in front of her – that is until she comes upon strangers going her way plus a barrier with villagers hurling stones at them.<br /><br />Caitrin is desperate and holds her own and request lodgings for the night. The villagers are not savages and they offer Caitrin what help they can, but they also warn her of the curse of the Tor and gives her some dire warnings about what goes on in the house up on the hill - the home of the chieftain of the Tor itself.<br /><br />Within twenty-four hours Caitrin is under the crumbling roof of the house on the hill and there is more there than the villagers feared in residence, and even more than she herself would have imagine even possible. <br /><br />This crumbling fortress is home to Anluan – the last of his line and the only one who has any control of the malevolent army that is the curse of the Tor. Anluan is the guardian of this curse, a century old and he needs someone to help him sort out what remains of his family history, Caitrin is capable and ready – but Anluan was just not prepared for Caitrin. <br /><br />As days and night passes and the curse draws it shroud around the Tor, Anluan and Caitrin finds that they need each other – Anluan for the courage that only Caitrin can give him and Caitrin finds everything in Anluan that she admires about a man plus she is determined to do all she can for the century old residents of the Tor. Their life is fated to disaster even before they have had a chance, because no matter how much Caitrin wishes for Anluan to be the man she wishes him to be Anluan has had his entire life and the voices to become set in one mode – defeat; Anluan would rather push Caitrin away before he allows the curse of his family to befall her.<br /><br />HEART’S BLOOD is everything that I expect a good fantasy to be – the setting is dark, the characters are such that they saw into me and I just can’t look away. The storylines are numerous and many and they all roll and tip over each other vying for dominance, but as all good story tellers does – Ms Marillier reigns then in with descriptive words lengthy scenes and enough mystery to keep me going.<br /><br />The story revolves around a century old curse that has not only crippled a village but an entire family has fallen foul of its evil arms. <br /><br />Caitrin comes along searching for her own path to self confidence but finds herself taking an even braver step that not only give to Anluan the one thing he had lost – Hope, but she gives an entire set of people the first ray of sunshine they have ever experience in a century.<br /><br />Then there is Anluan, the broken man – literally and figuratively. Without even knowing him, I was intrigued by him – he acted like he had the weight of the world on his shoulders and in some ways he did. As with men reared in that time – Anluan have high expectation of himself and finds himself wanting, it was a pleasure to watch him see himself through someone else’s eyes and it was like a flower opening - the end product was a force to be reckoned with.<br /><br />There is most definitely shades of Beauty and the Beast here – but Caitrin’s and Anluan romance is not one that rushes up on them and it was not expected to be so – their love was a calling and it feeds off the changing seasons, the sighing of their hearts, the wish for best and the hope that each will be the best of themselves. <br /><br />The setting of HEART’S BLOOD is 12th century Ireland and I love everything about that period – the savagery of it, the superstitious-ness of the people, the way they love with their entire being and the fact that life and death are but a whisper and it’s literally survival of the fitness and the craftiest. Marillier describes the period beautifully – I was there, I saw, I felt and I did not want to leave.<br /><br />This book is a character driven book, with not only the main protags capturing my heart, but life long friends making the journey worthwhile. Then there was the cursed people wanting just the pleasure of sleep and villagers who aptly knew the meaning of sticking with the devil you know than the one who wants to overrun the Tor boundaries. <br /><br />The storylines were suited to the time, there was no big drama – it was treachery, unfair play, power play and some neat scenes of rolling back the years to give me a look at the past, to see how it stacked up against the present and made me dig deep down for that hope for the future.<br /><br />If you like books that will stand the test of time, about characters that refuse to die, gothic in it’s feel – dark and malevolent in it’s evil but with a pace that suits the time, creeping, crawling and then in the clear light of day you can’t look away – this is the book for you.<br /><br />I totally enjoyed this journey and I am hoping this is not the last visit that Ms. Marillier takes me on to Whistling Tor. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="390621843099406708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14831369895924466708">Buddy read with Bookish buddies! I loved this tale, you have to warm up to it but its very caring, gentle and mysterious. This is my first book by Juliet Marillier and I love her writing style, its detailed, has a classic vibe to it and flows smoothly!<br/><br/>Heart's Blood is loosely based on Beauty and the Beast. Its told from a first person POV, so in the beginning it seems very rammbly! But you know with every start of a new story you need warming up and getting to know the person in the story. It al</span>
  <span id="freeText14831369895924466708" style="display:none">Buddy read with Bookish buddies! I loved this tale, you have to warm up to it but its very caring, gentle and mysterious. This is my first book by Juliet Marillier and I love her writing style, its detailed, has a classic vibe to it and flows smoothly!<br /><br />Heart's Blood is loosely based on Beauty and the Beast. Its told from a first person POV, so in the beginning it seems very rammbly! But you know with every start of a new story you need warming up and getting to know the person in the story. It also contains ghosts and other scary things, has magic and romance. Its a love story, but the real kind nothing too overdone. It really invests in character growth, overcoming fears and believing in yourself. Beautiful really haha.<br /><br />I recommend it if you like this kind of historical fantasy, cant wait to read more by the author :)</span>

<div id="review_96990149" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96990149" />
    <a title="Karith Amel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2783481-karith-amel"><img alt="Karith Amel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1272207203p2/2783481.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96990149?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karith Amel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karith Amel" href="/user/show/2783481-karith-amel">Karith Amel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451462930" href="/book/show/6391467-heart-s-blood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2783481-karith-amel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96990149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16707094085435763030">There are things I enjoyed about this book. The general idea was intriguing, and under the hands of a deft author could have been powerful. However, Marillier shows none of her old inclination to apply herself to the painstaking creation of subtle characters, eloquent dialogue, or moments heavy with meaning. Where did the magic of Daughter of the Forest go, where each word sung of stories beyond itself, and every silence was heavy with things unsaid?<br/><br/>The chemistry between the two main characters </span>
  <span id="freeText16707094085435763030" style="display:none">There are things I enjoyed about this book. The general idea was intriguing, and under the hands of a deft author could have been powerful. However, Marillier shows none of her old inclination to apply herself to the painstaking creation of subtle characters, eloquent dialogue, or moments heavy with meaning. Where did the magic of Daughter of the Forest go, where each word sung of stories beyond itself, and every silence was heavy with things unsaid?<br /><br />The chemistry between the two main characters was non-existent; their love a thing of hasty craftsmanship, that we must accept because we're told it's true, rather than seeing and feeling it for ourselves. The dialogue, besides being preachy and empty, was often completely disconnected and impossible to follow. Whatever the thought process of the characters that led them to such disconnected statements, they were not communicated to the reader. I begin to wonder if one of the reasons Daughter of the Forest is so profound is that Sorcha speaks so little. She watches, and she listens, and the silence must speak for her. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16707094085435763030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PXEZAaMuUC010HcLoXcQj0fHNjkZAk44F9+GrB/VlVnujy5SUavnc8MaDLuB2+dkSUqR9nANme4+LN4QHZftYg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dz2R8ljMYEAIualnDsN4hoN+ip5wkikcILHdZ6KAbd2kw6ahqknXHv5z0tcub49tjfMtURmd/soJQoXboMIV5g==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3928118812497586158">Juliet Marillier was born in Dunedin, New Zealand and grew up surrounded by Celtic music and stories. Her own Celtic-Gaelic roots inspired her to write her first series, the Sevenwaters Trilogy. Juliet was educated at the University of Otago, where she majored in music and languages, graduating BA and Bachelor of Music (Hons). Her lifelong interest in history, folklore and mythology has had a majo</span>
  <span id="freeText3928118812497586158" style="display:none">Juliet Marillier was born in Dunedin, New Zealand and grew up surrounded by Celtic music and stories. Her own Celtic-Gaelic roots inspired her to write her first series, the Sevenwaters Trilogy. Juliet was educated at the University of Otago, where she majored in music and languages, graduating BA and Bachelor of Music (Hons). Her lifelong interest in history, folklore and mythology has had a major influence on her writing.<br /><br />Juliet is the author of twenty-one historical fantasy novels for adults and young adults, as well as a book of short fiction. Juliet's novels and short stories have won many awards. <br /><br />Juliet lives in a 110 year old cottage in a riverside suburb of Perth, Western Australia. When not writing, she tends to her small pack of rescue dogs. She also has four adult children and eight grandchildren. Juliet is a member of the druid order OBOD (the Order of Bards, Ovates and Druids.)<br /></span>
